				<div class="minerva__subtitle"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=EBay_Inc.&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="EBay Inc.">EBay Inc.</a>)</span></div>

			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0"><p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>

<p>

<span style="font-size: small;"><span id="coordinates"><a href="/wiki/Geographic_coordinate_system" title="Geographic coordinate system">Coordinates</a>: <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=EBay&amp;params=37.2952_N_121.926_W_type:landmark_region:US-CA"><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">37°17′43″N</span> <span class="longitude">121°55′34″W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">37.2952°N 121.9260°W</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">37.2952; -121.9260</span></span></span></a></span></span></span>
<span></span>
</p>
<p><b>eBay Inc.</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/iː/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">iː</span><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/eɪ/: 'a' in 'face'">eɪ</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">EE</span>-bay</i></a>) is an American <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational</a> <a href="/wiki/E-commerce" title="E-commerce">e-commerce</a> corporation based in <a href="/wiki/San_Jose,_California" title="San Jose, California">San Jose, California</a>, that facilitates <a href="/wiki/Consumer_to_consumer" class="mw-redirect" title="Consumer to consumer">consumer-to-consumer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Business_to_consumer" class="mw-redirect" title="Business to consumer">business-to-consumer</a> sales through its website. eBay was founded by <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Omidyar" title="Pierre Omidyar">Pierre Omidyar</a> in the Fall of 1995, and became a notable success story of the <a href="/wiki/Dot-com_bubble" title="Dot-com bubble">dot-com bubble</a>. eBay is a multibillion-dollar business with operations in about 30 countries, as of 2011.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The date of the event predicted near this tag has passed. (August 2019)">needs update</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-Global_Trade:_1._Finding_International_Items_On_eBay_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Global_Trade:_1._Finding_International_Items_On_eBay-2">[2]</a></sup> The company manages the eBay website, an <a href="/wiki/Online_auction" title="Online auction">online auction</a> and shopping website in which people and businesses buy and sell a wide variety of <a href="/wiki/Goods_and_services" title="Goods and services">goods and services</a> worldwide. The website is free to use for buyers, but sellers are charged fees for listing items after a limited number of free listings, and again when those items are sold.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p><table class="infobox vcard" style="width:22em"><caption class="fn org">eBay Inc.</caption><tbody><tr><td colspan="2" class="logo" href="#cite_note-10-K-1">[1]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Equity_(finance)" title="Equity (finance)">Total equity</a></span></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><img alt="Decrease" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/11px-Decrease2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Decrease" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300"> <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$6.281 billion</span> <span style="font-size:85%;">(2018)</span><sup id="cite_ref-10-K_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10-K-1">[1]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;">Number of employees</div></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;">~14,000 <span style="font-size:85%;">(December 2018)</span><sup id="cite_ref-10-K_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10-K-1">[1]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><a href="/wiki/Subsidiary" title="Subsidiary">Subsidiaries</a></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><a href="/wiki/Auction_Co." title="Auction Co.">Auction Co.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kijiji" title="Kijiji">eBayClassifieds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kijiji" title="Kijiji">Kijiji</a>, <a href="/wiki/IBazar" title="IBazar">iBazar</a>, <a href="/wiki/GittiGidiyor" class="mw-redirect" title="GittiGidiyor">GittiGidiyor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gumtree" title="Gumtree">Gumtree</a>, <a href="/wiki/G-Market" title="G-Market">G-Market</a>, <a href="/wiki/StubHub" title="StubHub">StubHub</a>, <a href="/wiki/Half.com" title="Half.com">Half.com</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marktplaats.nl" title="Marktplaats.nl">Marktplaats.nl</a>, Qoo10.jp</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;">Website</th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.ebay.com">www<wbr></wbr>.ebay<wbr></wbr>.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table><p>In addition to eBay's original <a href="/wiki/Auction" title="Auction">auction</a>-style sales, the website has evolved and expanded to include: instant "Buy It Now" shopping; shopping by <a href="/wiki/Universal_Product_Code" title="Universal Product Code">Universal Product Code</a>, <a href="/wiki/ISBN" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN">ISBN</a>, or other kind of <a href="/wiki/Stock_Keeping_Unit" class="mw-redirect" title="Stock Keeping Unit">SKU</a> number (via <a href="/wiki/Half.com" title="Half.com">Half.com</a>, which was shut down in 2017); online classified advertisements (via <a href="/wiki/Kijiji" title="Kijiji">Kijiji</a>, or eBay Classifieds); online event ticket trading (via <a href="/wiki/StubHub" title="StubHub">StubHub</a>); and other services. eBay previously offered online money transfers as part of its services (via <a href="/wiki/PayPal" title="PayPal">PayPal</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Skype_and_PayPal_–_A_Different_Set_of_Rules_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skype_and_PayPal_%E2%80%93_A_Different_Set_of_Rules-4">[4]</a></sup> which was a wholly owned subsidiary of eBay from 2002 to 2015).<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none"><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(1)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2><section class="mf-section-1 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-1">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="1990s">1990s</span></h3>
<p>The AuctionWeb was founded in <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a> on September 3, 1995, by French-born <a href="/wiki/Iranian-American" class="mw-redirect" title="Iranian-American">Iranian-American</a> computer programmer <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Omidyar" title="Pierre Omidyar">Pierre Omidyar</a> as part of a larger personal site.<sup id="cite_ref-cohen_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cohen-6">[6]</a></sup> One of the first items sold on AuctionWeb was a broken <a href="/wiki/Laser_pointer" title="Laser pointer">laser pointer</a> for $14.83. Astonished, Omidyar contacted the winning bidder to ask if he understood that the laser pointer was broken. In his responding email, the buyer explained: "I'm a collector of broken laser pointers."<sup id="cite_ref-el_history_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-el_history-7">[7]</a></sup> It soon became the first <a href="/wiki/Online_auction" title="Online auction">online auction</a> site allowing person-to-person transactions, which led to a mass volume of <a href="/wiki/Online_transactions" class="mw-redirect" title="Online transactions">online transactions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bunnell_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bunnell-8">[8]</a></sup></p><p>Reportedly, eBay was simply a hobby for Omidyar until his Internet service provider informed him he would need to upgrade to a business account due to the high volume of traffic to his website. The resulting price increase (from $30/month to $250) prompted him to start charging those who used eBay, which was not met with any animosity.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> It did result in the hiring of Chris Agarpao as eBay's first additional employee to process mailed checks coming in for fees.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pomidyarji.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Pomidyarji.jpg/220px-Pomidyarji.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3078" data-file-height="2280"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 163px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Pomidyarji.jpg/220px-Pomidyarji.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="163" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pomidyarji.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Pierre_Omidyar" title="Pierre Omidyar">Pierre Omidyar</a>, founder and chairman of eBay</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Skoll" title="Jeffrey Skoll">Jeffrey Skoll</a> was hired as the first new president of the company in early 1996. In November 1996, the <a href="/wiki/Ecommerce_platform" class="mw-redirect" title="Ecommerce platform">E-Commerce platform</a> entered into its first third-party licensing deal, with a company called Electronic Travel Auction, to use SmartMarket Technology to sell plane tickets and other travel products. Growth was phenomenal; in January 1997 the site hosted 2,000,000 auctions, compared with 250,000 during the whole of 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p><p>The company officially changed the name of its service from AuctionWeb to eBay in September 1997. Originally, the site belonged to Echo Bay Technology Group, Omidyar's consulting firm. Omidyar had tried to register the domain name echobay.com, but found it already taken by the <a href="/wiki/Echo_Bay_Mines" title="Echo Bay Mines">Echo Bay Mines</a>, a gold mining company,<sup id="cite_ref-Echobay_Partners_LTD_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Echobay_Partners_LTD-11">[11]</a></sup> so he shortened it to his second choice, eBay.com.<sup id="cite_ref-The_history_of_ebay_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_history_of_ebay-12">[12]</a></sup> In 1997 the company received $6.7 million in funding from the venture capital firm <a href="/wiki/Benchmark_Capital" class="mw-redirect" title="Benchmark Capital">Benchmark Capital</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-eBoys:_The_First_Inside_Account_of_Venture_Capitalists_at_Work_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eBoys:_The_First_Inside_Account_of_Venture_Capitalists_at_Work-13">[13]</a></sup></p><p><a href="/wiki/Meg_Whitman" title="Meg Whitman">Meg Whitman</a> was hired by the board as eBay president and <a href="/wiki/CEO" class="mw-redirect" title="CEO">CEO</a> in March 1998. At the time, the company had 30 employees,<sup id="cite_ref-eBay_founder_factchecks_John_McCain_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eBay_founder_factchecks_John_McCain-14">[14]</a></sup> half a million users and revenues of $4.7 million in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> In 2001, eBay had the largest userbase of any <a href="/wiki/E-commerce" title="E-commerce">e-commerce</a> site.<sup id="cite_ref-Bunnell_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bunnell-8">[8]</a></sup></p><p>The frequently repeated story that eBay was founded to help Omidyar's fiancée trade <a href="/wiki/Pez" title="Pez">Pez</a> candy dispensers were fabricated by a <a href="/wiki/Public_relations" title="Public relations">public relations</a> manager, <a href="/wiki/Mary_Lou_Song" title="Mary Lou Song">Mary Lou Song</a>, in 1997 to interest the media, which were not interested in the company's previous explanation about wanting to create a "<a href="/wiki/Perfect_market" class="mw-redirect" title="Perfect market">perfect market</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-Berkun2010_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Berkun2010-16">[16]</a></sup> This was revealed in Adam Cohen's book, <i>The Perfect Store</i> (2002),<sup id="cite_ref-cohen_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cohen-6">[6]</a></sup> and confirmed by eBay.<sup id="cite_ref-Berkun2010_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Berkun2010-16">[16]</a></sup></p><p>After eBay went public, both Omidyar and Skoll became instant billionaires. eBay's target share price of $18 was all but ignored as the price went to $53.50 on the first day of trading.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p><p>The Pez dispenser myth generated enormous amounts of publicity and led to some of eBay's most explosive early growth among toy collectors. However, at the time, <a href="/wiki/Beanie_Babies" title="Beanie Babies">Beanie Babies</a> (manufactured by <a href="/wiki/Ty,_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="Ty, Inc.">Ty, Inc.</a>) were the leader in the toy category and the most difficult brand to find in retail stores. Beanie Babies quickly became the dominant product on eBay, accounting for 10% of all eBay listings in 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-DarkSide_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DarkSide-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BeaniesFortune_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BeaniesFortune-19">[19]</a></sup></p><p>While eBay was still a privately held company, two major factors contributed to its growing market share:
</p>
<ul><li>The growing <a href="/wiki/Beanie_Babies#Collectibility" title="Beanie Babies">collectibility of Beanie Babies</a> in the mid-1990s – collectors internationally were trying to complete their collection of Beanie Babies</li>
<li>Ty producing the <a href="/wiki/Ty_Inc.#First_business-to-consumer_Website" class="mw-redirect" title="Ty Inc.">first business-to-consumer Web site</a> - the original Ty Web site contained an online trading post where people could trade their Beanie Babies; however, the trading post was overwhelmed with unsortable listings, creating a legitimate demand for a more efficient online system to buy and trade Beanie Babies in the secondary market<sup id="cite_ref-DarkSide_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DarkSide-18">[18]</a></sup></li></ul><p>As a result, eBay provided a user-friendly interface to search for specific Beanie Babies that collectors were searching for.
</p><p>On September 21, 1998, eBay went public.<sup id="cite_ref-eBay_Inc._-_MSN_Fact_Sheet_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eBay_Inc._-_MSN_Fact_Sheet-20">[20]</a></sup> In the risk factors section of the annual report filed with the <a href="/wiki/US_Securities_and_Exchange" class="mw-redirect" title="US Securities and Exchange">US Securities and Exchange Commission</a> in 1998, Omidyar notes eBay's dependence on the continued strength of the Beanie Babies market.<sup id="cite_ref-DarkSide_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DarkSide-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="2000s">2000s</span></h3>
<p>As the company expanded product categories beyond collectibles into almost any saleable item, business grew quickly.<sup id="cite_ref-el_history_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-el_history-7">[7]</a></sup>  In 2000, eBay had 12 million registered users and a cyberinventory of more than 4.5 million items on sale on any given day.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup>  In February 2002 the company purchased iBazar, a similar European auction web site founded in 1998,<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> and then bought <a href="/wiki/PayPal" title="PayPal">PayPal</a> on October 3, 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p><p>By early 2008 the company had expanded worldwide, counting hundreds of millions of registered users as well as 15,000 employees and revenues of almost $7.7 billion. After nearly ten years at eBay, Whitman decided to enter politics. On January 23, 2008, the company announced that Whitman would step down on March 31, 2008, and <a href="/wiki/John_Donahoe" title="John Donahoe">John Donahoe</a> was selected to become president and CEO.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Whitman remained on the board of directors and continued to advise Donahoe through 2008. In late 2009 eBay completed the sale of <a href="/wiki/Skype" title="Skype">Skype</a> for $2.75 billion, but still owned 30% equity in the company.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="2010s">2010s</span></h3>
<p>In 2012 <a href="/wiki/High-Tech_Employee_Antitrust_Litigation" title="High-Tech Employee Antitrust Litigation">eBay was charged</a> by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Justice" title="United States Department of Justice">United States Department of Justice</a> with entering into non-solicitation agreements with other technology companies involving their highly skilled employees.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p><p>On September 30, 2014, eBay announced it would spin off PayPal into a separate publicly traded company, a demand made nine months prior by activist hedge fund magnate <a href="/wiki/Carl_Icahn" title="Carl Icahn">Carl Icahn</a>. The spinoff completed on July 18, 2015. eBay's then chief executive, John Donahoe, stepped down from that role.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Flipkart and eBay entered into a strategic partnership in 2017 under which eBay Inc acquired a 5.44% stake in Flipkart in exchange for its eBay India business for $211 Mn and a $514 Mn cash investment. As part of the partnership, Flipkart decided to use the eBay's platform for global outsourcing.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p><p>On January 31, 2018, eBay announced that they would replace PayPal as its primary payments provider with Netherlands-based start-up <a href="/wiki/Adyen" title="Adyen">Adyen</a>. The transition was set to be completed by 2021, but PayPal would remain an acceptable payment option on the site until further notice.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p><p>On July 31, 2019, the company acquired a 5.59 percent stake in Paytm Mall.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p><p>On September 25, 2019, it was announced that <a href="/wiki/Devin_Wenig" title="Devin Wenig">Devin Wenig</a> would be stepping down as eBay's CEO, and that <a href="/wiki/Scott_Schenkel" title="Scott Schenkel">Scott Schenkel</a>, senior vice president and chief financial officer since 2015, had been appointed as the interim CEO.<sup id="cite_ref-CNBC_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CNBC-33">[33]</a></sup> On April 13, 2020, it was announced that <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Iannone" title="Jamie Iannone">Jamie Iannone</a> would become the CEO on April 27.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(2)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_affairs">Corporate affairs</span></h2><section class="mf-section-2 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-2">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Board_of_directors">Board of directors</span></h3>
<p>As of October 2019 the board of directors was as follows:<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Thomas_J._Tierney" title="Thomas J. Tierney">Thomas J. Tierney</a>, co-founder of the <a href="/wiki/Bridgespan_Group" title="Bridgespan Group">Bridgespan Group</a>, Chairman of eBay since March 2003</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fred_D._Anderson" title="Fred D. Anderson">Fred D. Anderson</a>, former managing director of <a href="/wiki/Elevation_Partners" title="Elevation Partners">Elevation Partners</a>, director of eBay since July 2003</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tony_Bates" title="Tony Bates">Anthony Bates</a>, CEO of <a href="/wiki/Genesys_(company)" title="Genesys (company)">Genesys</a></li>
<li>Adriane M. Brown, advisor at <a href="/wiki/Intellectual_Ventures" title="Intellectual Ventures">Intellectual Ventures</a>, LLC</li>
<li>Jesse Cohn, Head of U.S. Equity Activism at <a href="/wiki/Elliott_Management_Corporation" title="Elliott Management Corporation">Elliott Management Corporation</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Diana_Farrell" title="Diana Farrell">Diana Farrell</a>, CEO of <a href="/wiki/JPMorgan_Chase" title="JPMorgan Chase">JPMorgan Chase Institute</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Logan_Green" title="Logan Green">Logan Green</a>, CEO of <a href="/wiki/Lyft" title="Lyft">Lyft</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bonnie_Hammer" title="Bonnie Hammer">Bonnie Hammer</a>, Chairman, <a href="/wiki/NBC_Universal" class="mw-redirect" title="NBC Universal">NBC Universal</a></li>
<li>Kathleen Mitic, CEO of Sitch, Inc.</li>
<li>Matt Murphy, CEO of <a href="/wiki/Marvell_Technology_Group" title="Marvell Technology Group">Marvell Technology Group</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pierre_Omidyar" title="Pierre Omidyar">Pierre Omidyar</a>, director since 1996 and chairman of eBay from May 1996 to May 2015</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Paul_Pressler" title="Paul Pressler">Paul Pressler</a>, Partner at <a href="/wiki/Clayton,_Dubilier_%26_Rice" title="Clayton, Dubilier &amp; Rice">Clayton, Dubilier &amp; Rice</a>, LLC</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bob_Swan" title="Bob Swan">Bob Swan</a>, CEO of <a href="/wiki/Intel_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Intel Corporation">Intel Corporation</a></li>
<li>Perry Traquina, CEO of <a href="/wiki/Wellington_Management_Company" title="Wellington Management Company">Wellington Management Company</a></li></ul><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Logo">Logo</span></h3>
<p>In September 2012, eBay introduced a new logo set in the <a href="/wiki/Univers" title="Univers">Univers</a> typeface, but using a thinner variation of it,<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> installed on the website on October 10, 2012. It replaced the logo with a thicker variation of Univers which had been used since its establishment in 1995.  An all red, eBay logo with the same type set was also introduced to be used temporarily for various holidays.
</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed"><li class="gallerybox" style="width: 98.666666666667px"><div style="width: 98.666666666667px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 96.666666666667px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:EBay_former_logo.svg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/EBay_former_logo.svg/145px-EBay_former_logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="97" height="40" data-file-width="1543" data-file-height="642"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 97px;height: 40px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/EBay_former_logo.svg/145px-EBay_former_logo.svg.png" data-alt="" data-width="97" data-height="40" data-srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/EBay_former_logo.svg/217px-EBay_former_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/EBay_former_logo.svg/289px-EBay_former_logo.svg.png 2x"> </span></a></div></div>

<p>2012–present
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
</ul><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Profit_and_transactions">Profit and transactions</span></h3>
<p>eBay generates revenue by a complex system of fees for services, listing product features, and a <i>final value fee</i> for sales proceeds by sellers. As of 2019 the US-based eBay.com charges <a href="/wiki/United_States_Dollar" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Dollar">$</a>0.35 as an insertion fee for a basic listing without any adornments. The final value fee is 10-12% of the total amount of the sale, which is the price of the item plus shipping charges.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Reduced final value fees are available to business registered customers. Other eBay websites follow a similar fee structure, but with different cost charges.
</p><p>Under US law before 2018, a state cannot require sellers located outside the state to collect a <a href="/wiki/Sales_tax" title="Sales tax">sales tax</a>, which made making purchases on eBay more attractive to American buyers. Sellers that operate as a business do follow state tax regulations on eBay transactions.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-eBay_Guides_-_Tickets_Buying_Guide_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eBay_Guides_-_Tickets_Buying_Guide-39">[39]</a></sup> Since 2018, changes to tax law in the United States force eBay (and other large marketplaces) to collect sales tax on any eBay purchase shipped to certain states.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p><p>The company's business strategy includes increasing international trade.<sup id="cite_ref-eBay_Inc._-_eBay_Inc._Outlines_Global_Business_Strategy_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eBay_Inc._-_eBay_Inc._Outlines_Global_Business_Strategy-41">[41]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_brand_that_auctioned_the_www:_eBay_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_brand_that_auctioned_the_www:_eBay-42">[42]</a></sup> eBay has already expanded to over <a href="#International">two dozen countries</a>, including China and India. Strategic international expansion has failed in Taiwan and Japan, where <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!" title="Yahoo!">Yahoo!</a> had a head start, and New Zealand, where <a href="/wiki/Trade_Me" title="Trade Me">Trade Me</a> is the dominant online auction website. eBay also notably failed in China due to competition from local rival <a href="/wiki/Taobao" title="Taobao">Taobao</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> eBay entered the Chinese market in 2002 and shut down its Chinese site in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> In India, eBay's operations came to a halt<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> after it sold off its <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> operations<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> to country's largest ecommerce company <a href="/wiki/Flipkart" title="Flipkart">Flipkart</a>, in the latter's $1.4Bn fundraise,<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> where eBay was a participant.
</p><p>In its Q1 2008 results, total payment volume via PayPal increased 17%, but of the eBay auction site it was up 61%.<sup id="cite_ref-Q1_eBay_earnings_call_April_16,_2008_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Q1_eBay_earnings_call_April_16,_2008-48">[48]</a></sup></p><p>For most listing categories, eBay sellers are permitted to offer a variety of payment systems such as Escrow.com,<sup id="cite_ref-eBay_Inc_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eBay_Inc-49">[49]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/PayPal" title="PayPal">PayPal</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Paymate&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Paymate (page does not exist)">Paymate</a>, Propay, and Skrill.<sup id="cite_ref-Accepted_Payments_Policy_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Accepted_Payments_Policy-50">[50]</a></sup> Propay and Skrill were banned effective September 27, 2015, citing low usage.<sup id="cite_ref-ecom-ebayban_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ecom-ebayban-51">[51]</a></sup></p><p>Escrow.com is eBay's approved <a href="/wiki/Escrow" title="Escrow">escrow</a> site. The transactions processed through Escrow.com largely are in relation to eBay Motors; however, they are not restricted to this type of listing.<sup id="cite_ref-eBay_Inc_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eBay_Inc-49">[49]</a></sup></p><p>eBay runs an affiliate program under the name eBay Partner Network.<sup id="cite_ref-eBay_Partner_Network_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eBay_Partner_Network-52">[52]</a></sup> eBay affiliate marketers were originally paid a percentage of the eBay seller's transaction fees, with commissions ranging from 50% to 75% of the fees paid for an item purchased. In October 2009, eBay changed to an affiliate payout system that it calls Quality Click Pricing, in which affiliates are paid an amount determined by an undisclosed algorithm. The total earnings amount is then divided by the number of clicks the affiliate sent to eBay and is reported as Earnings Per Click, or EPC. In October 2013, ePN launched a new pricing model. The new model is more transparent and is based on category-level base commission rates with bonuses available for referring new and reactivated buyers.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated5_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated5-53">[53]</a></sup></p><p>On April 18, 2012, eBay reported a 29% Q1 revenue increase to $3.3 billion compared to their Q1 in 2011. Net income was reported to be at $570 million for the quarter.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p><p>For the fiscal year 2017, eBay reported losses of US$1.016 billion, with annual revenue of US$9.567 billion, an increase of 6.6% over the previous fiscal cycle. eBay's shares traded at over $35 per share, and its market capitalization was valued at over US$27.2 billion in October 2018.
</p>
