</td></tr></tbody></table><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_record">Environmental record</span></h3>
<p>On May 8, 2008, eBay announced the opening of its newest building on the company's North Campus in <a href="/wiki/San_Jose,_California" title="San Jose, California">San Jose</a>, which is the first structure in the city to be built from the ground up to <a href="/wiki/Leadership_in_Energy_and_Environmental_Design" title="Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design">LEED</a> Gold standards.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-69">[69]</a></sup> The building, the first the company had built in its 13-year existence, uses an array of 3,248 solar panels, spanning 60,000 square feet (5,600 m<sup>2</sup>), and providing 650 kilo<a href="/wiki/Watt" title="Watt">watts</a> of power to eBay's campus.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-70">[70]</a></sup> The array can supply 15–18% of the company's total energy requirements, reducing the amount of <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gases</a> that would be produced to create that energy by other means.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-70">[70]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/SolarCity" title="SolarCity">SolarCity</a>, the company responsible for designing the array, estimates that the solar panels installed on eBay's campus will prevent 37 million pounds of <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a> from being released into the environment as a result of replaced power production over the next three decades. Creating an equivalent impact to remove the same amount of carbon dioxide from the atmosphere would require planting 322 acres (1.30 km<sup>2</sup>) of trees.
</p><p>The design of the building also incorporates other elements to reduce its impact on the environment. The building is equipped with a lighting system that detects natural ambient light sources and automatically dims artificial lighting to save 39% of the power usually required to light an office building. eBay's newest building also reduces demand on local water supplies by incorporating an eco-friendly irrigation system, and low-flow showerheads and faucets. Even during construction, more than 75% of the waste from construction was recycled. eBay also runs buses between San Francisco and the San Jose campus to reduce the number of commuting vehicles.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-69">[69]</a></sup> In 2014, eBay and several other Oregon businesses signed the Oregon Business Climate Declaration to promote local job growth and slow carbon pollution.<sup id="cite_ref-bizjournal_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bizjournal-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Acquisitions">Acquisitions</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_acquisitions_by_eBay" title="List of acquisitions by eBay">List of acquisitions by eBay</a></div>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="PayPal">PayPal</span></h4>
<p>On October 3, 2002, PayPal became a wholly owned subsidiary of eBay.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> Its corporate headquarters were sited in <a href="/wiki/San_Jose,_California" title="San Jose, California">San Jose, California</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-samuels2012_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-samuels2012-73">[73]</a></sup> United States at eBay's North First Street satellite office campus. On September 30, 2014, eBay Inc. announced the divestiture of PayPal as an independent company, which was completed on July 20, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Craigslist">Craigslist</span></h4>
<p>In the summer of 2004, eBay acknowledged that it had acquired 25% of classified listings website <a href="/wiki/Craigslist" title="Craigslist">Craigslist</a>. Former Craigslist executive Phillip Knowlton was the seller, and he insisted that his former employer was aware of his plans to divest his holdings. Initially, eBay assured Craigslist that eBay would not ask Craigslist to change the way it did business.
</p><p>In March 2005, eBay launched the classifieds service <a href="/wiki/Kijiji" title="Kijiji">Kijiji</a>. In April 2008, eBay sued Craigslist to "safeguard its four-year financial investment", claiming that in January 2008, Craigslist took actions that "unfairly diluted eBay's economic interest by more than 10%".<sup id="cite_ref-EBay_sues_Craigslist_ad_website_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EBay_sues_Craigslist_ad_website-75">[75]</a></sup> Craigslist countersued in May 2008 "to remedy the substantial and ongoing harm to fair competition" that Craigslist claimed was constituted by eBay's actions as a Craigslist shareholder.<sup id="cite_ref-Craigslist_strikes_back_at_eBay_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Craigslist_strikes_back_at_eBay-76">[76]</a></sup> In September 2010, Delaware Judge <a href="/wiki/William_B._Chandler_III" title="William B. Chandler III">William Chandler</a> ruled that the actions of Craigslist were unlawful and that the actions were taken by Craigslist founders <a href="/wiki/Jim_Buckmaster" title="Jim Buckmaster">Jim Buckmaster</a> and <a href="/wiki/Craig_Newmark" title="Craig Newmark">Craig Newmark</a> had "breached their fiduciary duty of loyalty", and restored eBay's stake in the company to 28.4% from a diluted level of 24.85%.<sup id="cite_ref-Market_Watch_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Market_Watch-77">[77]</a></sup> However, the judge dismissed eBay's objection to a staggered board provision, citing that Craigslist has the right to protect its own trade secrets.<sup id="cite_ref-eBay_Gets_Partial_Win_in_Craigslist_Poison_Pill_Lawsuit_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eBay_Gets_Partial_Win_in_Craigslist_Poison_Pill_Lawsuit-78">[78]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ruling_Restores_Ebay's_Stake_in_Craigslist_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ruling_Restores_Ebay's_Stake_in_Craigslist-79">[79]</a></sup> eBay spokesman Michael Jacobson stated "We are very pleased that the court gave eBay what it sought from the lawsuit."<sup id="cite_ref-Market_Watch_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Market_Watch-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Skype">Skype</span></h4>
<p>In October 2005, eBay Inc. acquired <a href="/wiki/Skype_Technologies" title="Skype Technologies">Skype Technologies</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> developer of the <a href="/wiki/Skype" title="Skype">Skype</a> <a href="/wiki/VoIP" class="mw-redirect" title="VoIP">VoIP</a> and <a href="/wiki/Instant_messaging" title="Instant messaging">Instant messaging</a> service, significantly expanding its customer base to more than 480 million registered users worldwide. eBay later sold a majority stake in Skype in November 2009, while retaining a minority investment.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> This eventually led to the sale of the entire Skype business to <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> for $8.5 billion in May 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="StubHub">StubHub</span></h4>
<p>StubHub's acquisition by eBay was announced in January 2007 for a reported $310 million.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ShellyVermaat2008_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ShellyVermaat2008-84">[84]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AP0107_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AP0107-85">[85]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/CNN_Money" class="mw-redirect" title="CNN Money">CNN Money</a>, 2007 was a very successful year for the company, handling five million individual transactions, more than in the previous six years combined of its history.<sup id="cite_ref-Fekete2010_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fekete2010-86">[86]</a></sup> Staffing at StubHub had increased to 350 workers by the time of the sale.<sup id="cite_ref-AP0107_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AP0107-85">[85]</a></sup> Eight months after the acquisition, StubHub reached an exclusive agreement with <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> (MLB).<sup id="cite_ref-Fekete2010_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fekete2010-86">[86]</a></sup> They get a piece of the 25% in commissions StubHub earns on either end of a sale. <a href="/wiki/Ticketmaster" title="Ticketmaster">Ticketmaster</a> filed a lawsuit against StubHub and eBay in 2007, alleging "intentional interference" with Ticketmaster's contractual rights.<sup id="cite_ref-Inc.2007_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Inc.2007-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Corrigon">Corrigon</span></h4>
<p>In October 2016, eBay acquired <a href="/wiki/Corrigon" title="Corrigon">Corrigon</a>, a visual search engine, for less than $30 million.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Qoo10.jp">Qoo10.jp</span></h4>
<p>In April 2018, eBay acquired the Japanese division of <a href="/wiki/Qoo10" title="Qoo10">Qoo10</a>, a market place driven by Giosis and having the 4th GMV in Japan, for a reported $573 million.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> With the close of the transaction, eBay also has relinquished its investment in Giosis’ non-Japanese businesses.  This acquisition expands eBay's footprint in Japan, one of the largest e-commerce markets in the world. eBay made an initial investment in Giosis Pte. Ltd. in 2010.  Since then, Giosis has established dynamic marketplace businesses across Asia. eBay's Japan business, including Giosis’ Japan business, will report into Jooman Park, senior vice president of eBay's Asia Pacific region.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(3)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Use_for_data_analysis">Use for data analysis</span></h2><section class="mf-section-3 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-3">
<p>eBay is a publicly visible market which has attracted interest from economists, who have used it to analyze aspects of buying and selling behavior, auction formats, etc., comparing them with previous theoretical and empirical findings.
</p><p>Computer information systems researchers have also shown interest in eBay. Michael Goul, Chairman of the Computer Information Systems department of the <a href="/wiki/W._P._Carey_School_of_Business" title="W. P. Carey School of Business">W. P. Carey School of Business at Arizona State University</a>, published an academic case based on eBay's <a href="/wiki/Big_data" title="Big data">big data</a> management and use in which he discusses how eBay is a data-driven company that processes 50 <a href="/wiki/Petabyte" title="Petabyte">petabytes</a> of data a day.<sup id="cite_ref-knowwpc_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-knowwpc-91">[91]</a></sup></p><p>eBay uses a system that allows different departments in the company to check out data from their data mart into sandboxes for analysis. According to Goul, eBay has already experienced significant business successes through its data analytics. eBay employs 5,000 data analysts to enable data-driven decision making.<sup id="cite_ref-knowwpc_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-knowwpc-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Third_party">Third party</span></h3>
<p>In 2006 the accounting software company <a href="/wiki/Intuit" title="Intuit">Intuit</a> launched a web-based donation tracking service called ItsDeductible. The service uses data from eBay to help users assign a <a href="/wiki/Market_value" title="Market value">market value</a> to the items they donate.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Visual_search">Visual search</span></h3>
<p>In July 2017 eBay released an image search capability allowing users to find listings on the site that match an item depicted in a photo, using artificial intelligence and machine learning technologies.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="GCHQ">GCHQ</span></h3>
<p>UK's <a href="/wiki/GCHQ" title="GCHQ">GCHQ</a> has a suite of tools for monitoring target use of eBay, named ELATE.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Items">Items</span></h3>
<p>Millions of <a href="/wiki/Collectable" title="Collectable">collectibles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Interior_design" title="Interior design">decor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Home_appliance" title="Home appliance">appliances</a>, computers, <a href="/wiki/Furniture" title="Furniture">furnishings</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tool" title="Tool">equipment</a>, <a href="/wiki/Domain_name" title="Domain name">domain names</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> vehicles, and other miscellaneous items are listed, bought, or sold daily on eBay. In 2006, eBay launched its Business &amp; Industrial category, breaking into the industrial surplus business. Generally, anything can be auctioned on the site as long as it is not illegal and does not violate the eBay Prohibited and Restricted Items policy.<sup id="cite_ref-Prohibited_and_Restricted_Items_-_Overview_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Prohibited_and_Restricted_Items_-_Overview-96">[96]</a></sup> Services and <a href="/wiki/Intangible_asset" title="Intangible asset">intangibles</a> can be sold, too. Large international companies, such as <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a>, sell their newest products and offer services on eBay using competitive auctions and fixed-priced storefronts. Separate eBay sites such as eBay US and eBay UK allow the users to trade using the local currency. Software developers can create applications that integrate with eBay through the <a href="/wiki/EBay_API" title="EBay API">eBay API</a> by joining the eBay Developers Program.<sup id="cite_ref-eBay_Developers_Program_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eBay_Developers_Program-97">[97]</a></sup> In June 2005, there were more than 15,000 members in the eBay Developers Program, comprising a broad range of companies creating software applications to support eBay buyers and sellers as well as eBay Affiliates.
</p><p>Numerous government and police agencies<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> around the world now use eBay as well as traditional <a href="/wiki/Auction" title="Auction">auctions</a> to dispose of seized and confiscated goods.
</p><p>Controversy has arisen over certain items put up for bid. For instance, in late 1999 a man offered one of his <a href="/wiki/Kidney" title="Kidney">kidneys</a> for auction on eBay, attempting to profit from the potentially lucrative (and, in the United States, illegal) market for <a href="/wiki/Organ_transplant" class="mw-redirect" title="Organ transplant">transplantable human organs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-kidney_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kidney-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:PayPal_San_Jose_Headquarters.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/PayPal_San_Jose_Headquarters.jpg/200px-PayPal_San_Jose_Headquarters.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 200px;height: 150px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/PayPal_San_Jose_Headquarters.jpg/200px-PayPal_San_Jose_Headquarters.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="200" data-height="150" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:PayPal_San_Jose_Headquarters.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>eBay North First Street satellite office campus (home to PayPal)</div></div></div>
<p>Beginning in August 2007, eBay required listings in "Video Games" and "Health &amp; Beauty" to accept its payment system <a href="/wiki/PayPal" title="PayPal">PayPal</a> and sellers could only accept PayPal for payments in the category "Video Games: Consoles".<sup id="cite_ref-August_10,_2007,_10:38 am_BST_post_to_eBay_announcement_board_by_eBay's_staff_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-August_10,_2007,_10:38_am_BST_post_to_eBay_announcement_board_by_eBay's_staff-100">[100]</a></sup> Starting January 10, 2008, eBay said sellers can only accept PayPal as payment for the categories "Computing &gt; Software", "Consumer Electronics &gt; MP3 Players", "Wholesale &amp; Job Lots &gt; Mobile &amp; Home Phones", and "Business, Office &amp; Industrial &gt; Industrial Supply / MRO".<sup id="cite_ref-December_21,_2007_12:10 pm_GMT_General_announcement_by_eBay_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-December_21,_2007_12:10_pm_GMT_General_announcement_by_eBay-101">[101]</a></sup> eBay announced that starting in March 2008, eBay had added to this requirement that all sellers with fewer than 100 feedbacks must offer PayPal and no <a href="/wiki/Merchant_account" title="Merchant account">merchant account</a> may be used as an alternative.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-eBay_February_2008_announcement_board_posted_on_February_28,_2008_02:49 pm_GMT_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eBay_February_2008_announcement_board_posted_on_February_28,_2008_02:49_pm_GMT-103">[103]</a></sup> This is in addition to the requirement that all sellers from the United Kingdom have to offer PayPal.<sup id="cite_ref-eBay_announcement_March_24,_2008_09:00 am_GMT_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eBay_announcement_March_24,_2008_09:00_am_GMT-104">[104]</a></sup></p><p>Further, and as noted below, it was a requirement to offer PayPal on all listings in Australia and the UK. In response to concerns expressed by the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Competition_and_Consumer_Commission" title="Australian Competition and Consumer Commission">Australian Competition and Consumer Commission</a>, however, eBay has since removed the policy on the eBay.com.au website requiring sellers to offer PayPal as a payment option.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ebay_express.png" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b5/Ebay_express.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="40" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="200" data-file-height="40"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 200px;height: 40px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b5/Ebay_express.png" data-alt="" data-width="200" data-height="40" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ebay_express.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>eBay Express logo</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EBayTorontoOffice.JPG" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/EBayTorontoOffice.JPG/220px-EBayTorontoOffice.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="332" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="4928"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 332px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/EBayTorontoOffice.JPG/220px-EBayTorontoOffice.JPG" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="332" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EBayTorontoOffice.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>eBay Office in Toronto, Canada</div></div></div>
<p>On April 24, 2006, eBay opened its new eBay Express site, which was designed to work like a standard Internet shopping site for consumers with United States addresses.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> Before it closed in 2008, selected eBay items were mirrored on eBay Express, where buyers used a traditional digital shopping cart to purchase from multiple sellers.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> The UK version was launched to eBay members in mid-October 2006, but on January 29, 2008, eBay announced its intention to close the site.<sup id="cite_ref-January_2008_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-January_2008-107">[107]</a></sup> The German version, eBay Express Germany,<sup id="cite_ref-eBay_-_eine_der_größten_deutschen_Shopping-Websites_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eBay_-_eine_der_gr%C3%B6%C3%9Ften_deutschen_Shopping-Websites-108">[108]</a></sup> was also opened in 2006 and closed in 2008.
</p><p>At the 2008 eBay Developer's Conference, eBay announced the Selling Manager Applications program (SM Apps).<sup id="cite_ref-eBay_Developer's_Conference_Highlights_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eBay_Developer's_Conference_Highlights-109">[109]</a></sup> The program allows approved developers to integrate their applications directly into the eBay.com interface.<sup id="cite_ref-Selling_Manager_Applications_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Selling_Manager_Applications-110">[110]</a></sup> The applications created by developers are available for subscription by eBay members who also subscribe to Selling Manager.
</p><p>eBay maintains a number of specialty sites including the discussion boards, groups, answer center, chat rooms, and reviews and guides. eBay's mobile offerings include <a href="/wiki/Short_message_service" class="mw-redirect" title="Short message service">SMS</a> alerts, a <a href="/wiki/Wireless_Application_Protocol" title="Wireless Application Protocol">WAP</a> site, <a href="/wiki/Java_ME" class="mw-redirect" title="Java ME">Java ME</a> clients, and mobile applications for <a href="/wiki/Windows_Phone" title="Windows Phone">Windows Phone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android OS</a>, and Apple iPhone.
</p><p>The initiative <a href="/wiki/Choice_in_eCommerce" title="Choice in eCommerce">Choice in eCommerce</a> was founded on May 8, 2013, by several online retailers in <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>, Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> The cause was, in the view of the initiative, sales bans and online restrictions by individual manufacturers. The dealers felt cut off from their main sales channel and thus deprived them the opportunity to use online platforms like <a href="/wiki/Amazon.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon.com">Amazon</a>, eBay, or <a href="/wiki/Rakuten" title="Rakuten">Rakuten</a> in a competitive market for the benefit of their customers.
</p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Unusual_items">Unusual items</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Unusual_eBay_listings" title="Unusual eBay listings">Unusual eBay listings</a></div>
<p>Many unusual items have been placed for sale on eBay, including at least two previously undiscovered species, including the <i><a href="/wiki/Coelopleurus_exquisitus" title="Coelopleurus exquisitus">Coelopleurus exquisitus</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Sea_urchin" title="Sea urchin">sea urchin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-120">[120]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Insect_expert_discovers_new_species_on_eBay_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Insect_expert_discovers_new_species_on_eBay-121">[121]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Prohibited_or_restricted_items">Prohibited or restricted items</span></h4>
<p>In its earliest days, eBay was nearly unregulated. However, as the site grew, it became necessary to restrict or prohibit auctions for various items. Note that some of the restrictions relate to eBay.com (the US site), while other restrictions apply to specific European sites (such as Nazi paraphernalia). Regional laws and regulations may apply to the seller or the buyer. Generally, if the sale or ownership of an item is regulated or prohibited by one or more states, eBay will not permit its listing. Among the hundred or so banned or restricted categories:
</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Tobacco" title="Tobacco">Tobacco</a> (tobacco-related items and collectibles are accepted.)<sup id="cite_ref-Tobacco_policy_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tobacco_policy-122">[122]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alcoholic_beverages" class="mw-redirect" title="Alcoholic beverages">Alcohol</a> (alcohol-related collectibles, including sealed containers, as well as some wine sales by licensed sellers are allowed, some sites such as ebay.com.au allow licensed liquor sales)<sup id="cite_ref-Alcohol_policy_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alcohol_policy-123">[123]</a></sup> (eBay announced September 21, 2012, it will begin removing listings for beer and liquor from its site after a story was aired on <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a> series <i><a href="/wiki/20/20_(U.S._TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="20/20 (U.S. TV series)">20/20</a></i>.)<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Prohibition_(drugs)" class="mw-redirect" title="Prohibition (drugs)">Drugs</a> and drug paraphernalia<sup id="cite_ref-Drugs_and_drug_paraphernalia_policy_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Drugs_and_drug_paraphernalia_policy-125">[125]</a></sup></li>
<li>Items that "promote or glorify hatred, violence, racial, sexual, or religious intolerance, or promote organizations with such views". This includes <a href="/wiki/Nazi_memorabilia" title="Nazi memorabilia">Nazi paraphernalia</a>, although there are exceptions to this rule for Nazi items such as stamps, letters, and envelopes displaying Nazi postmarks (must comply with the currency and stamp policy)</li>
<li>Items depicting the <a href="/wiki/Confederate_battle_flag" class="mw-redirect" title="Confederate battle flag">Confederate battle flag</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ars-confederateban_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ars-confederateban-126">[126]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bootleg_recording" title="Bootleg recording">Bootleg recordings</a><sup id="cite_ref-Bootleg_recordings_policy_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bootleg_recordings_policy-127">[127]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Firearm" title="Firearm">Firearms</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ammunition" title="Ammunition">ammunition</a> (as of January 1, 1999),<sup id="cite_ref-Firearms,_weapons,_and_knives_policy_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Firearms,_weapons,_and_knives_policy-128">[128]</a></sup> including any parts that could be used to assemble a firearm as well as (as of July 30, 2007) any firearm part that is required for the firing of a gun, including bullet slugs, brass casings and shells, slides, cylinders, magazines, firing pins, trigger assemblies, etc. Various types of knives are also forbidden.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Police" title="Police">Police</a> and <a href="/wiki/Emergency_service" title="Emergency service">emergency service</a> vehicular warning equipment such as red or blue lights and sirens (antique or collectible items are exempt)</li>
<li>Intentionally soiled <a href="/wiki/Undergarment" title="Undergarment">underwear</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Panty_fetishism" class="mw-redirect" title="Panty fetishism">Panty fetishism</a>) and dirty used clothing<sup id="cite_ref-Used_clothing_policy_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Used_clothing_policy-129">[129]</a></sup></li>
<li>Forged, illegal, stolen, or confidential documents, which include <a href="/wiki/Passports" class="mw-redirect" title="Passports">passports</a>, <a href="/wiki/Social_Security_(United_States)" title="Social Security (United States)">Social Security</a> cards, <a href="/wiki/Drivers_license" class="mw-redirect" title="Drivers license">drivers licenses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Voter_registration_card" class="mw-redirect" title="Voter registration card">voter registration cards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Birth_certificate" title="Birth certificate">birth certificates</a>, school documents, <a href="/wiki/Medical_record" title="Medical record">medical records</a>, financial information, government <a href="/wiki/License_plate" class="mw-redirect" title="License plate">license plates</a>, or government classified information documents. Any item that is used to modify documents is also restricted.<sup id="cite_ref-Government_documents,_IDs,_and_licenses_policy_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Government_documents,_IDs,_and_licenses_policy-130">[130]</a></sup></li>
<li>Human <a href="/wiki/Human_body" title="Human body">body parts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organ_(anatomy)" title="Organ (anatomy)">organs</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cadaver" title="Cadaver">remains</a> (with an exception for <a href="/wiki/Skeleton" title="Skeleton">skeletons</a> and <a href="/wiki/Skull" title="Skull">skulls</a> for scientific study, provided they are not <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">Native American</a> in origin)<sup id="cite_ref-Human_remains_and_body_parts_policy_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Human_remains_and_body_parts_policy-131">[131]</a></sup></li>
<li>Live animals (with certain exceptions)<sup id="cite_ref-animals_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-animals-132">[132]</a></sup></li>
<li>Certain copyrighted works or trademarked items<sup id="cite_ref-Rules_about_intellectual_property_–_overview_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rules_about_intellectual_property_%E2%80%93_overview-133">[133]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lottery" title="Lottery">Lottery</a> tickets, <a href="/wiki/Sweepstakes" class="mw-redirect" title="Sweepstakes">sweepstakes</a> tickets, or any other <a href="/wiki/Gambling" title="Gambling">gambling</a> items.<sup id="cite_ref-Slot_machines_policy_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Slot_machines_policy-134">[134]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Military_hardware" class="mw-redirect" title="Military hardware">Military hardware</a> such as working <a href="/wiki/Weapons" class="mw-redirect" title="Weapons">weapons</a> or <a href="/wiki/Explosives" class="mw-redirect" title="Explosives">explosives</a> with the exception of <a href="/wiki/Demilitarized" class="mw-redirect" title="Demilitarized">demilitarized</a> <a href="/wiki/Vehicles" class="mw-redirect" title="Vehicles">vehicles</a>.</li>
<li>Any object of <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iranian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuban</a>, or <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korean</a> origin.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li>Enriched <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">uranium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plutonium" title="Plutonium">plutonium</a>, and other <a href="/wiki/Fissile_material" title="Fissile material">fissile material</a>.</li>
<li>Certain categories of <a href="/wiki/Human_sexuality" title="Human sexuality">sexually oriented</a> material, which must be listed in the "Adult Only" category,<sup id="cite_ref-adult_only_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-adult_only-135">[135]</a></sup> notwithstanding certain items prohibited:<sup id="cite_ref-adult_only_135-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-adult_only-135">[135]</a></sup><ul><li><a href="/wiki/Child_pornography" title="Child pornography">Child pornography</a></li>
<li>Materials deemed <a href="/wiki/Obscene" class="mw-redirect" title="Obscene">obscene</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Bestiality" class="mw-redirect" title="Bestiality">bestiality</a>, <a href="/wiki/Necrophilia" title="Necrophilia">necrophilia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rape" title="Rape">rape</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coprophilia" title="Coprophilia">coprophilia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Incest" title="Incest">incest</a></li>
<li>Used <a href="/wiki/Sex_toys" class="mw-redirect" title="Sex toys">sex toys</a></li>
<li>Services including any sexual activity</li>
<li>Links to sites that contain prohibited items</li>
<li>Adult products that are delivered digitally</li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Virtuality" class="mw-redirect" title="Virtuality">Virtual</a> items from <a href="/wiki/Massively_multiplayer_online_game" title="Massively multiplayer online game">massively multiplayer online games</a>, restrictions that vary by country<sup id="cite_ref-Digitally_delivered_goods_policy_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Digitally_delivered_goods_policy-136">[136]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-eBay_bans_the_auction_of_in-game_items_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eBay_bans_the_auction_of_in-game_items-137">[137]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ivory_trade" title="Ivory trade">Ivory</a> products<sup id="cite_ref-animals_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-animals-132">[132]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Knives" class="mw-redirect" title="Knives">Knives</a>, other than some <a href="/wiki/Cutlery" title="Cutlery">cutlery</a>, are prohibited in the UK following the criminal importation into the UK (by BBC Watchdog researchers) of several knives that were already illegal to own or import under existing UK legislation. The ban also includes empty leather knife <a href="/wiki/Scabbard" title="Scabbard">scabbards</a> if they are listed under the category of "knives" on one of the eBay sites<sup id="cite_ref-bbcknifeban_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcknifeban-138">[138]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fortune-telling" title="Fortune-telling">Fortune-telling</a> and <a href="/wiki/Witchcraft" title="Witchcraft">witchcraft</a>-related services<sup id="cite_ref-Sale_of_tarot_readings_and_spells_banned_on_eBay_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sale_of_tarot_readings_and_spells_banned_on_eBay-139">[139]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Souls" class="mw-redirect" title="Souls">Souls</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ghost" title="Ghost">ghosts</a>, and other "items whose existence cannot be verified" are prohibited.<sup id="cite_ref-no_item_listing_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-no_item_listing-140">[140]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Norton_DJ's_charity_ghost_sale_spirited_off_eBay_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Norton_DJ's_charity_ghost_sale_spirited_off_eBay-141">[141]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-soul_selling_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-soul_selling-142">[142]</a></sup></li>
<li>Many other items are either wholly prohibited or restricted in some manner.<sup id="cite_ref-Prohibited_and_restricted_items_–_overview_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Prohibited_and_restricted_items_%E2%80%93_overview-143">[143]</a></sup></li></ul></div>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Bidding">Bidding</span></h3>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Auction-style_listings">Auction-style listings</span></h4>
<p>Bidding on eBay (old or new)'s auction-style listing is called <a href="/wiki/Proxy_bid" title="Proxy bid">proxy bidding</a> and is essentially equivalent to a <a href="/wiki/Vickrey_auction" title="Vickrey auction">Vickrey auction</a> (sealed-bid), with the following exceptions.
</p>
<ul><li>The winning bidder pays the second-highest bid plus one bid increment amount (that is, some small predefined amount relative to the bid size), instead of simply the highest bid. However, since the bid increment amounts are relatively insignificant compared to the bid size, they are not considered from a strategic standpoint.<sup id="cite_ref-eBay's_explanation_of_bid_increments_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eBay's_explanation_of_bid_increments-144">[144]</a></sup></li>
<li>The highest bidder's bid is sealed, as in a <a href="/wiki/Vickrey_auction" title="Vickrey auction">Vickrey auction</a>, but the current winning bid (second highest plus one increment) is displayed throughout the auction to allow <a href="/wiki/Price_discovery" title="Price discovery">price discovery</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup></li>
<li>Because eBay's auction-style listings are sealed-bid, it is usually to all bidders' advantage that bids are made only at the very end of the auction (except for an initial minimum bid, that cancels out a "Buy It Now" option, or prevents the seller from ending the listing early). Early bids will usually not increase the bidder's chance of winning the auction, and will often raise the item's final price (winning bid) for the eventual winner.</li>
<li>eBay also allows sellers to offer a "Buy it Now" price that will end the auction immediately. The Buy It Now price is available until someone bids on the item, or until the reserve price is met. When the Buy It Now option disappears, the auction-style listing proceeds normally.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup></li></ul><h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Seller_ratings">Seller ratings</span></h4>
<p>In 2008, eBay implemented a system of seller ratings with four categories. Buyers are asked to rate the seller in each of these categories with a score of one to five, with five being the highest rating. Unlike the overall feedback rating, these ratings are anonymous; neither sellers nor other users learn how individual buyers rated the seller. The listings of sellers with a rating of 4.3 or below in any of the four rating categories appear lower in search results. Power Sellers are required to have scores in each category above 4.5.<sup id="cite_ref-February_2008_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-February_2008-147">[147]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-January_20081_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-January_20081-148">[148]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Upcoming_Changes_to_Feedback_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Upcoming_Changes_to_Feedback-149">[149]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Fees_2008_Overview_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fees_2008_Overview-150">[150]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-January_20082_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-January_20082-151">[151]</a></sup></p><p>In a reversal of roles, on January 24, 2010, Auctionbytes.com held an open survey in which sellers could rate eBay, as well as competing auction and marketplace sites.<sup id="cite_ref-survey_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-survey-152">[152]</a></sup> In the survey, users were asked to rank 15 sites based on five criteria: profitability, customer service, communication, ease of use, and recommendation.
</p><p>eBay was ranked 13th,<sup id="cite_ref-auctionbytes13_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auctionbytes13-153">[153]</a></sup> after other large sites such as <a href="/wiki/Amazon.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon.com">Amazon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Craigslist" title="Craigslist">Craigslist</a>, as well as lesser-known selling sites such as <a href="/w/index.php?title=Atomic_Mall&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Atomic Mall (page does not exist)">Atomic Mall</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=ECRATER&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="ECRATER (page does not exist)">eCRATER</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ruby_Lane" title="Ruby Lane">Ruby Lane</a>. In individual category rankings, eBay was rated the worst of all the 15 sites on customer service and communication, and average on ease of use. Some respondents stated they would have given eBay a rating of 10, three to five years ago. eBay was rated twelfth out of fifteen in the Recommended Selling Venue category.
</p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Charity_auctions">Charity auctions</span></h4>
<p>Using <a href="/wiki/MissionFish" title="MissionFish">MissionFish</a> as an arbiter, eBay allows sellers to donate a portion of their auction proceeds to a charity of the seller's choice.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> The program is called eBay Giving Works in the US, and eBay for Charity<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> in the UK. eBay provides a partial refund of seller fees for items sold through charity auctions.<sup id="cite_ref-eBay_Giving_Works_fee_credits_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eBay_Giving_Works_fee_credits-156">[156]</a></sup> As of March 4, 2010, $154 million has been raised for US nonprofits by the eBay Community since eBay Giving Works began in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup></p><p>Some high-profile charity auctions have been advertised on the eBay home page.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> As of June 2010, the highest successful bid on a single item for charity was for the annual "Power Lunch"<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> with investor <a href="/wiki/Warren_Buffett" title="Warren Buffett">Warren Buffett</a> at the famous <a href="/wiki/Smith_%26_Wollensky" title="Smith &amp; Wollensky">Smith &amp; Wollensky</a> Steakhouse in New York. The winning bid was $2.63 million with all of the proceeds going to the <a href="/wiki/Glide_Foundation" title="Glide Foundation">Glide Foundation</a>. The winning bidder was not made public, but was able to bring up to seven friends to the lunch. In 2012, a higher bid, of $3.46 million, also going to the Glide Foundation, won a lunch with Buffet.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> In 2016 an anonymous bidder won a $3.45 million lunch with Warren Buffett and the money raised from the auction was given to Glide Foundation.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup></p><p>The previous highest successful bid on a single item for charity was for a letter<sup id="cite_ref-eBay_Update:_High_Bidder_on_Reid_Letter_Will_Own_Historic_Document_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eBay_Update:_High_Bidder_on_Reid_Letter_Will_Own_Historic_Document-162">[162]</a></sup> sent to Mark P. Mays, CEO of <a href="/wiki/Clear_Channel_Communications" class="mw-redirect" title="Clear Channel Communications">Clear Channel</a> (parent company of <a href="/wiki/Premiere_Radio_Networks" class="mw-redirect" title="Premiere Radio Networks">Premiere Radio Networks</a> the production company that produces <i><a href="/wiki/The_Rush_Limbaugh_Show" title="The Rush Limbaugh Show">The Rush Limbaugh Show</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Glenn_Beck_Program" title="Glenn Beck Program">Glenn Beck Program</a></i>) by Senator <a href="/wiki/Harry_Reid" title="Harry Reid">Harry Reid</a> and forty other <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a> senators, complaining about comments made by conservative talk show host <a href="/wiki/Rush_Limbaugh" title="Rush Limbaugh">Rush Limbaugh</a>. The winning bid was $2,100,100, with all of the proceeds going to the Marine Corps-Law Enforcement Foundation, benefiting the education of children of men and women who have died serving in the armed forces. The winning bid was matched by Limbaugh in his largest charity donation to date.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup></p><p>In 2007; eBay Canada partnered with Montreal-based digital branding agency CloudRaker to develop a campaign to raise money for Sainte-Justine children's hospital in Montreal. They aligned themselves with Internet phenomenon <a href="/wiki/T%C3%AAtes_%C3%A0_claques" title="Têtes à claques">Têtes à claques</a> to create an eBay auction based on popular T-A-C character Uncle Tom, an infomercial host who pitches absurd products. eBay and CloudRaker reproduced Uncle Tom's imaginary products, The Body Toner Fly Swatter, The Willi Waller Potato Peeler, and the LCD Shovel and sold them online. In six weeks, they raised $15,000 for Hôpital St-Justine with one fly swatter, one potato peeler, and one shovel, a world record. The Body Toner Fly Swatter sold for $8,600, the Willi Waller Potato Peeler sold for $3,550, and the LCD Shovel sold for $2,146.21.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Shipping">Shipping</span></h3>
<p>During auction setup, eBay provides shipping-method choices to sellers: ordinary mail, <a href="/wiki/Express_mail" title="Express mail">express mail</a>, and/or courier service. The seller may choose to offer only one shipping method to buyers, or the seller may offer buyers a choice of options.
</p><p>Very-low-value items shipped directly from China are sometimes shipped by <a href="/wiki/Surface_mail" title="Surface mail">surface mail</a> (seamail), which is inexpensive but takes one to two months.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> If the buyer is in a hurry, he or she might be able to pay an extra fee to upgrade to second-class <a href="/wiki/Surface_Air_Lifted" title="Surface Air Lifted">Surface Air Lifted</a> shipping or to first-class <a href="/wiki/Airmail" title="Airmail">airmail</a> shipping.
</p><p>Since 2012, eBay has been enlisting sellers into its "Global Shipping Program". If a seller uses the program, non-domestic buyers pay a fee to <a href="/wiki/Pitney_Bowes" title="Pitney Bowes">Pitney Bowes</a>. The seller sends the item to a Pitney Bowes facility in the US (or the UK), which then forwards it to the buyer, taking care of all international shipping requirements. The program is claimed to enhance the product selection available to international buyers.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(4)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversy_and_criticism">Controversy and criticism</span></h2><section class="mf-section-4 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-4">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_eBay" title="Criticism of eBay">Criticism of eBay</a></div>
<p>Common eBay criticisms involve the policy of requiring the use of <a href="/wiki/PayPal" title="PayPal">PayPal</a> for payments and concerns over fraud, forgeries and intellectual property violations in auction items.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> There are also issues of how negative feedback after an auction can offset the benefits of using eBay as a trading platform.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> eBay has been criticized for not paying UK taxes: the <i>Sunday Times</i> reported in October 2012 that eBay paid only £1.2m in tax on sales of over £800m.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="2014_security_breach">2014 security breach</span></h3>
<p>On May 21, 2014, the company revealed that the consumer database of usernames, passwords, phone numbers, and physical addresses had been breached between late February and early March. Users were advised to change their passwords; to expedite this, a "change password" feature was added to profiles of users who had not yet done so. The <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Electronic_Army" title="Syrian Electronic Army">Syrian Electronic Army</a> took responsibility for the attack. The SEA said that even though the hack revealed millions of users' banking details to them, they would not misuse the data. They had replaced the front pages of the websites with their own logo, called "<a href="/wiki/Website_defacement" title="Website defacement">Defacing</a>" in technical terms. The hack caused eBay's share price to crash in intra-day trade as a result of the breach of security.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(5)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2><section class="mf-section-5 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-5">
